    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't know if this is what you mean but there is a quote like that in The Last Kingdom. Unfortunately, I am reading the large print version where it<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't know if this is what you mean but there is a quote like that in The Last Kingdom. Unfortunately, I am reading the large print version where it is on pages 470-471. I guess you would find that quote about 4/5ths of the way through the book where Uthred is called to meet with Alfred at Werham.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1307749308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307749308" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307749308?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307749308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer93983284383955621">There is nothing I’d like to see more than Uhtred completely re-joining the Danes. I’d like to see him join forces with Ragnar Ragnarson. I’d like to see the two stood side by side in the shield wall. I’d like to see them smash Alfred’s forces and Uhtred plunge Serpents Breath into the heart of Wessex. But, alas, Alfred has Uhtred’s oath of loyalty and obedience. He may leave his side for a time, but it would never, and could never, be permanent. <br/><br/><b>A strong test of loyalty</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1434304286p8/1196148.jpg' width='400' height='240' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>However, when he accident</span>
  <span id="freeText93983284383955621" style="display:none">There is nothing I’d like to see more than Uhtred completely re-joining the Danes. I’d like to see him join forces with Ragnar Ragnarson. I’d like to see the two stood side by side in the shield wall. I’d like to see them smash Alfred’s forces and Uhtred plunge Serpents Breath into the heart of Wessex. But, alas, Alfred has Uhtred’s oath of loyalty and obedience. He may leave his side for a time, but it would never, and could never, be permanent. <br><br><b>A strong test of loyalty</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1434304286p8/1196148.jpg" width="400" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, when he accidently breaks a priest’s neck, when he tried to get him to shut up by punching him in the face, he is forced to flee from Alfred’s court. Despite the victory Uhtred has just granted Alfred, which literally saved his kingdom he is banished because he accidently kills a simple minded priest. Indeed, the men he has just saved call for his blood: the blood of the warrior without whom they would all be dead. Well, that’s gratitude for you. Who could blame Uhtred for finally trying to fulfil his heart’s desire? <br><br><i>I was without a lord. I was outcast. I was free. I was going Viking. </i><br><br>Unfortunately Uhtred has a soft spot for Alfred’s daughter. When she comes requesting his help he is forced to make, yet, another hard decision. He is torn between wanting to fight with his Danish brothers and the King he has sworn his service to. Alfred’s daughter reminds him of his oath, and one he also made to her in private. Uhtred is in a difficult situation because if he goes with her he may have to face his beloved friend Ragnar Ragnarson, which is a fate worse than death. How could Uhtred fight the man he loves for the man he hates?<br><br><b> Bad choices</b><br><br>I really don’t like Alfred the Great in this novel. He owes everything to Uhtred, as without him he would have lost his kingdom long ago, yet time and time again he rewards him with punishment. I cannot comprehend why Uhtred still fights for this man. He clearly cannot lead him to the retaking of his childhood home; he clearly cannot lead him to any serious wealth. And to top it all off he manipulates Uhtred into fighting for him in the most devious ways. If I was Uhtred, I would long have abandoned this King. I think he is a bad choice of a man to follow. <br><br>The thing I enjoy most about this series is the way it is narrated by an Uhtred who is looking back on his life. You can almost see the smile on the aged warrior’s face as he recalls the memories of his youth and the battles past. Also, you can hear his regret and the bad decisions he has made, and the decisions he would now make instead. I hope at the end of the series he finally gets his birth right, which will give the warrior a sense of peace and completion. He will have no more reason to raid or fight someone else’s enemies. He can be his own lord. <br><br>Overall, this is another great edition to the series. In this Uhtred gets the closest he has ever been to joining the Danes since he was among them in the beginning. I feel like the author has almost teased me with it in this novel; it’s like his shown us something that could have happened and then turned the novel back in on itself and showed us what will always happen. Damn you Bernard Cornwell for getting my foolish hopes up once again. <br><br><u> The Saxon Stories </u><br>1. <i>The Last Kingdom-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184243350?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A fine five stars</a><br>2. <i>The Pale Horsman-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186450906?type=review#rating_37274009" rel="nofollow noopener">A brilliant five stars</a><br>3.<i>Lords of the North-</i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199820612?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A vengeful four stars</a><br>4.<i>Sword Song- </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1224878875?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A familiar four stars</a><br>5.<i>The Burning Land-</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307749308?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A loyal five stars</a><br>6.<i> Death of Kings </i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1390733251?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A mighty five stars</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="93983284383955621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3435399429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3435399429" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3435399429?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3435399429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16082223388574973286">In The Burning Land, the fifth entry in The Saxon Stories, we follow the escapades of a 35 or 36-year-old Uhtred of Bebbanburg. He's still Alfred's oathman and has been residing in Lundune. The Danish warrior, and Uhtred's ex-servant Haesten is an everpresent nuisance, but in this novel, we are introduced to the leader and lover of another force of Danes who are being problematic and threatening Alfred's peace. Harald Bloodhair and Skade. Haesten informs Uhtred that Skade is Bloodhair's woman, b</span>
  <span id="freeText16082223388574973286" style="display:none">In The Burning Land, the fifth entry in The Saxon Stories, we follow the escapades of a 35 or 36-year-old Uhtred of Bebbanburg. He's still Alfred's oathman and has been residing in Lundune. The Danish warrior, and Uhtred's ex-servant Haesten is an everpresent nuisance, but in this novel, we are introduced to the leader and lover of another force of Danes who are being problematic and threatening Alfred's peace. Harald Bloodhair and Skade. Haesten informs Uhtred that Skade is Bloodhair's woman, bitch, lover, and sorceress. He also kindly warns Uhtred that "if you see her, my friend, you’ll want her. But she’ll nail your skull to her hall gable if she can." The Burning Land is about these Danish threats to Wessex and Mercia and the importance of oaths.<br /><br />Recently The Saxon Stories series has been my go-to choice when I couldn't decide between other books to read next. I find myself drifting back to them every 3rd or 4th book. My experiences with all of the stories so far have been 4 or 5-star reads and at approximately 300-pages I tend to race through these in under a week. The chapters here take about half an hour to read and I tended to devour 2 or 3 in a sitting. The Burning Land is more of the same of what has come before yet the series is nowhere near becoming stale, in fact, I'd say that as Uhtred is ageing his life experience and intelligence lead to really clever moments that are great to read. Such as a moment including bees and another with ships' sails.<br /><br />We still have battles, war councils, friendships, loyalty, and omens but, however much I have enjoyed the previous novels, I think this entry has been the perfect example of Cornwell's strengths as a writer put on display. There is still humour featured in The Burning Land when the scenarios permit it, as there is dread, fear, and hatred. Uhtred's utter loathing of Christianity is known throughout at least three nations and he doesn't let that up in this entry either, as can be seen in quotes such as the below:<br /><br />Folk tell their children that success lies in working hard and being thrifty, but that is as much nonsense as supposing that a badger, a fox and a wolf could build a church. The way to wealth is to become a Christian bishop or a monastery’s abbot and thus be imbued with heaven’s permission to lie, cheat and steal your way to luxury.<br /><br />Another highlight of The Saxon Stories is the rich and diverse cast of characters. Uhtred's first-person perspective presents a wide plethora of emotions depending on who he is discussing. Love for someone like Gisela, respect for someone like Steapa, loyalty for someone like Finan, admiration for someone like Æthelflæd, and detest for someone like Æthelred or any number of the gaggle of religious influencers.<br /><br />‘Æthelflæd remains your wife,’ I told him quietly, ‘but if she dies mysteriously, or if she sickens, or if I hear rumours of a spell cast against her, then I shall find you, cousin, and I shall suck the eyeballs out of your skull and spit them down your throat so you choke to death.’ I smiled. ‘Send your men to Lundene and keep your country.’<br /><br />If I hadn't received a review copy of one of my most anticipated reads of the year (R. F. Kuang's The Burning God) then I more than likely would have just carried on with this series. At this rate, I will have finished the books that are already out before the release of the final novel, Wolf Lord, on the 15th of October. My fellow reviewer Edward Gwynne's reviews of the later novels remain extremely positive so it looks like I am in for more fine reading experiences with Uhtred, Finan, Osferth et al. Uhtred is 35-36 during this novel, not much older than me, and he is still in the front row of the shield wall or the first over the palisades. I'm intrigued to see if, and how, that changes as he ages further, yet I predict his importance will not be diminished. I really can't wait to continue with Uhtred's adventure and know for sure that I will be back very soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16082223388574973286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1149802851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149802851" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149802851?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007219742" href="/book/show/3650343-the-burning-land">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149802851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8229895717878214362"><b>”“The gods are capricious, and I was about to amuse them. And Alfred was right. I was a fool.” </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Thor_by_Abrar_Ajmal_zpsd4d4a443.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413809i/815209._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo Thor_by_Abrar_Ajmal_zpsd4d4a443.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>The Mighty Thor</b><br/><br/>Uhtred, Lord of Bebbanburg, is an enigma. He is a man without a country, not only because England doesn’t yet exist in the 9th century, but he is also a man without a home. His uncle took his position as rightful heir to Bebbanburg when Uhtred’s father died. He does still call himself Lord of Bebbanburg, but it is from exile in the South. Uhtred is a Saxon, but he was raised by Vikin</span>
  <span id="freeText8229895717878214362" style="display:none"><b>”“The gods are capricious, and I was about to amuse them. And Alfred was right. I was a fool.” </b><br><br><a href="http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Thor_by_Abrar_Ajmal_zpsd4d4a443.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413809i/815209._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Thor_by_Abrar_Ajmal_zpsd4d4a443.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>The Mighty Thor</b><br><br>Uhtred, Lord of Bebbanburg, is an enigma. He is a man without a country, not only because England doesn’t yet exist in the 9th century, but he is also a man without a home. His uncle took his position as rightful heir to Bebbanburg when Uhtred’s father died. He does still call himself Lord of Bebbanburg, but it is from exile in the South. Uhtred is a Saxon, but he was raised by Vikings. He learned to fight like them and he also learned to worship like them. He wears a Thor’s amulet and insists on maintaining his pagan ways even though he has sworn an oath to fight and protect the most pious of Christian kings, Alfred the Great. <br><br>Alfred was once a man who enjoyed a good feast and a dalliance in the bed of a pretty girl. Osferth, his bastard son, exists because of one of those moments of pleasure. He is a constant reminder, like looking in a mirror, of Alfred’s days of illicit pleasure. <br><br>And then Alfred converted to Christianity.<br><br>He is tedious in his devotion. His knees are black and blue from hours of kneeling. His voice is parched from hours of keening prayers. His diet is feeble and bland. He is a sickly king, but he is strong in his devotion to his GOD who he believes will always give him victory. <br><br>Uhtred would disagree. Uhtred knows that Wessex still exists only because of his strong arm and his brilliant tactics on the battlefield. Alfred knows this too otherwise why would he tolerate a pagan among his most trusted advisors. <br><br>Alfred is King of Wessex, not king of England. As the North becomes saturated with more and more Northmen looking for land, women, and treasure he finds it more and more difficult to keep these pagan barbarians out of the Southern lands he commands. His only defense is Uhtred and the inability of the Vikings to organize. (Similar problem to what the Native Americans in North America had issues with.)<br><br>There is this constant push and pull between Alfred and Uhtred. Alfred wants to build churches. Uhtred wants to build fortifications. Their religions are diametrically opposed. <br><br><i>”Our gods prefer feasting. They live, Uhtred. They live and laugh and enjoy, and what does their god do? He broods, he’s vengeful, he scowls, he plots. He’s a dark and lonely god, Uhtred, and our gods ignore him. They are wrong.”</i><br><br>Frankly if Uhtred wants a future in England for his gods Thor and Odin he should put a sword through Alfred instead of working so assiduously to keep the King of the Christians alive. An oath is an oath and once given it must be upheld. <br><br>The Vikings are amassing for yet another invasion of Wessex. Alfred is sick and dying. Uhtred is ready to escape North the moment Alfred breathes his last. He still dreams of ruling Bebbanburg, but he will need treasure and men to do it. A sorceress named Skade is with the Vikings. She is a wild beauty who exudes a power over men that is detrimental to all. <br><br>Many women have mentioned to me who read Bernard Cornwell that he can’t write a flesh and blood woman character to save his life. His characterisations of women sometimes put me in mind of Michelangelo’s statues of females who really look like men with breasts. <br><br><a href="http://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/59d3775d-5dc1-4251-9943-41e392e57252_zpsea29c396.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420830888i/13274767.gif" alt=" photo 59d3775d-5dc1-4251-9943-41e392e57252_zpsea29c396.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>His female characters are split between those manly women, much prettier than the Michelangelo statues, who can fight and be one of the boys and the women that are serving as pleasure models or breeders. Although with the character of Aethelflaed, Alfred’s daughter, he might have an opportunity to write a woman that will finally depict a strong, capable, and thoughtful woman capable of ruling an empire. <br><br>Bernard Cornwell is a conduit to my memories of the many hours of pleasure I spent as a lad reading about lawmen with strapped down six-shooters, sword swinging barbarians, and gat carrying gumshoes. Cornwell is certainly a step up from the pulpy books of my youth. He decided to write these books because he didn’t feel that the British knew enough about the origins of their own country. In the 9th century, with the emergence of Alfred, it is also the beginnings of an island country who will eventually rule the waves and will come close to ruling the world. I’m many, many books behind reading the prolific writing of Cornwell, but there is a comfort in knowing that when I need one there will always be a stack of new ones to pick from. <br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8229895717878214362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_697679042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697679042" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697679042?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697679042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4342060262479965849">If reading this series doesn't make you wanna scream like this... <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://ledzeppelin.alexreisner.com/sound/isong.mp3'>http://ledzeppelin.alexreisner.com/so...</a> ...then I just don't know what will!<br/><br/><i>The Burning Land</i> continues Bernard Cornwell's bloodthirsty, battle-heavy and viciously violent viking saga. <br/><br/>England is still broken up into pieces. The Danes are threatening to overrun the land. Saxon King Alfred (later known as Alfred the Great) was holding on to Wessex and holding out hope of one day uniting the entire country under his banner. But need</span>
  <span id="freeText4342060262479965849" style="display:none">If reading this series doesn't make you wanna scream like this... <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ledzeppelin.alexreisner.com/sound/isong.mp3">http://ledzeppelin.alexreisner.com/so...</a> ...then I just don't know what will!<br /><br /><i>The Burning Land</i> continues Bernard Cornwell's bloodthirsty, battle-heavy and viciously violent viking saga. <br /><br />England is still broken up into pieces. The Danes are threatening to overrun the land. Saxon King Alfred (later known as Alfred the Great) was holding on to Wessex and holding out hope of one day uniting the entire country under his banner. But needs the help of fighting men like our anti-hero hero Uhtred of Bebbanburg.<br /><br />Though he's a pagan and acts like a Dane, Uhtred is actually a Saxon, who was raised by those viking Danes. He reluctantly works for Alfred, even if the piously Christian king and all his self-righteous priests get up Uhtred's nose. He's a fierce, skilled fighter who doesn't mind getting his hands dirty and his nose bloodied. It's what he's good at. However, he doesn't like to be anyone's lapdog, so any chance he gets, he heads north to threaten the impregnable fortress at Bebbanburg, his rightful seat of power, currently held by his usurping uncle. <br /><br />Cornwell is a dab hand at crafting this particular character. You'll find him in the long-running <i>Sharpe</i> series as the titular main character. Cornwell is also quite adept at writing very exciting and highly realistic historical fiction. You're in capable hands on both counts. I especially like that he includes afterwards of real history information at the end of these books to let you know the true story behind the fiction. In this one he admits to falsifying the character of a historical figure to fit his novel and goes on to give a recommendation for further and more correct reading on said figure. That's a conscientious writer for you!<br /><br /><i>The Burning Lands</i> is a particularly tight volume in this series. Each scene is meaningful and the action feels fast. Any lapse in the forward progress is a joy to read as Cornwell does his best to paint vivid settings and to portray all, from Saxon to Dane, man to woman and peasant to King. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4342060262479965849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>„Wyrd bið ful ãræd.“ – „Fate is inexorable.“</i>

Bernard Cornwell brought 9th century England alive for me.<br/><br/>* Unforgettable narrator. Uhtred of Bebbanburg is unapologetic and ruthless yet lovable and admirati</span>
  <span id="freeText10220977055895870602" style="display:none">Fast-paced and engaging, this series is still keeping its charm!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>„Wyrd bið ful ãræd.“ – „Fate is inexorable.“</i>
</blockquote><br>I had a super long review written for this series but I deleted the document accidentally so let me share with you at least some major points to explain my reasons for loving this series so much:<br><br>* Astonishing storytelling skills. Bernard Cornwell brought 9th century England alive for me.<br><br>* Unforgettable narrator. Uhtred of Bebbanburg is unapologetic and ruthless yet lovable and admiration worthy character with brilliant military strategic mind. He is a true hero!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497621564ra/23044089.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>* Complex and fascinating side characters that you will love to come back to.<br><br>* Constant philosophical battle between paganism and Christianity that depicts given period precisely.<br><br>* Well thought-out storyline and twists.<br><br>* War and fight scenes are chillingly realistic. I really felt like I was there with Uhtred, fighting every new enemy or being part of countless shield wars.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463241704ra/19097865.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, The Warrior Chronicles/Saxon Stories series (all 10 available books) is spectacular story with spectacular writing. It is one of the best historical fiction stories I have ever read and it is the perfect example of how to write engaging historical fiction series that never get boring or predictable!<br><br>Moreover, I loved author’s note at the end of every book where author explained which parts were based on historical facts and which parts of his novel he made up. <br><br>RECOMMENDED!</span>

<div id="review_2423343162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2423343162" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/155663-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581956036p2/155663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423343162?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/155663-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423343162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15996982318128518322">This is the fifth book in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43581-the-saxon-stories' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Saxon Stories</a> by Bernard Cornwell. I had listened to all of the previous books in the series in audiobook format. This is the first one that I read in print. I thought, before starting the book, that it would be dry because it was not being read by a narrator. But, I was wrong. The printed book is just as fun as the audiobooks. I am always amazed by the ingenuity that Bernard Cornwell inserts into the situations that befall the main character of the book, Uhtred. I </span>
  <span id="freeText15996982318128518322" style="display:none">This is the fifth book in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43581-the-saxon-stories" rel="nofollow noopener">The Saxon Stories</a> by Bernard Cornwell. I had listened to all of the previous books in the series in audiobook format. This is the first one that I read in print. I thought, before starting the book, that it would be dry because it was not being read by a narrator. But, I was wrong. The printed book is just as fun as the audiobooks. I am always amazed by the ingenuity that Bernard Cornwell inserts into the situations that befall the main character of the book, Uhtred. I have yet to be bored; every chapter is entertaining and a joy to read.<br /><br />The characters all seem so human. Sometimes they make wise decisions, while at other times they seem to be their own worst enemies. For example, Uhtred is usually making very good choices and strategies when he has sufficient time to think it all out. But when he is enraged, he can do the stupidest things. <br /><br />I applaud Bernard Cornwell's imagination and his wonderful story-telling ability. The battles, the enmities, and the friendships are all told so well, it is quite amazing to me. I highly recommend this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15996982318128518322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5660347813182627761">I am sad to report I can only give this one <b>3 Stars</b>...I really had high hopes for my return to the world of Uhtred of Bebbanburg and England of the late 9th Century. <br/><br/>The good points: 1) no one does a better battle scene than Cornwell and the battles here are pretty good; 2) Cornwell really paints a grim picture of life and it always seems accurate; 3) Cornwell skewers treacherous royalty and Christian priests with such skill (yet also portrays some as brave and likeable).<br/><br/>The bad: 1) Uhtred is pi</span>
  <span id="freeText5660347813182627761" style="display:none">I am sad to report I can only give this one <b>3 Stars</b>...I really had high hopes for my return to the world of Uhtred of Bebbanburg and England of the late 9th Century. <br /><br />The good points: 1) no one does a better battle scene than Cornwell and the battles here are pretty good; 2) Cornwell really paints a grim picture of life and it always seems accurate; 3) Cornwell skewers treacherous royalty and Christian priests with such skill (yet also portrays some as brave and likeable).<br /><br />The bad: 1) Uhtred is pissing me off. He has such clever strategy and tactics when supporting King Alfred's goals yet is so stupid when it come to his own goals (like recovering Bebbanburg or protecting his family); 2) Uhtred pretty much meanders aimlessly between battles while moping about his "fate". 3) Just didn't feel like the story was much advanced with this one.</span>

<div id="review_1197659542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1197659542" />
    <a title="Athena Shardbearer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159427-athena-shardbearer"><img alt="Athena Shardbearer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546027968p2/4159427.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1197659542?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060888749" href="/book/show/6806468-the-burning-land">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=having-book-babies">having-book-babies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=lord-markus-the-book-pusher">lord-markus-the-book-pusher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=do-want">do-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159427-athena-shardbearer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1197659542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6761550420665639636"><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"We are Danes, and we are Saxon, and we are warriors who love to fight. In our halls at night we chant the tales of men we have killed, of the women we have widowed, and of the children we have orphaned. So make your choice! Either give me a new song to sing or else lay down your weapons."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Oh Uhtred, chaos and mayhem follows you where ever you go. This far in the series and I'm starting to question the decisions that Uhtred makes and the people he makes promises to. Will he ever be happy, eve</span>
  <span id="freeText6761550420665639636" style="display:none"><br><blockquote>
  <i>"We are Danes, and we are Saxon, and we are warriors who love to fight. In our halls at night we chant the tales of men we have killed, of the women we have widowed, and of the children we have orphaned. So make your choice! Either give me a new song to sing or else lay down your weapons."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Oh Uhtred, chaos and mayhem follows you where ever you go. This far in the series and I'm starting to question the decisions that Uhtred makes and the people he makes promises to. Will he ever be happy, ever get what is rightfully his, ever really pick a side? Born Saxon and raised Dane he really has no idea which side to turn to and he's a rouge, doing what he feels he has to and sometimes that's not in his best interest. <br><br>Now, lets talk about the Saxon side. It gets harder and harder for me to like Alfred, and that's because of Uhtreds view of him. Yes, Alfred is a great ruler, he has a vision of what he wanted for his country and to unite it all under one kingdom, but that doesn't mean he isn't ruthless and using Uhtred for that gain. This is the biggest conflict for me in this series. I like Alfred then I hate him and on and on. Uhtred isn't any better, but I loves him. PERIOD.<br><br>What I enjoy most is the struggle at the beginning of what becomes a power nation and the tug of war between two religions and people. Pagans vs. Christians, Saxons vs. Danes and trying to find a way to rid the country of these heathens. It just shows how powerful Christianity becomes and the influence it has over the world. <br><br>This series just slipped into my favorites, I see myself rereading these years to come and I'm only halfway through this journey. We all know the outcome and who wins in the end, but I have to say that I'm a Dane. <br><br>Uhtred, come to the dark side(Danes), we have cookies!!!<br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363331i/714604.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1264265657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264265657" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264265657?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25786286-the-burning-land">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=not-a-bookclub-club">not-a-bookclub-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own-backlog">own-backlog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264265657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8788995583591499896"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Another enjoyable read in this series. These books are always quick reads that seem so packed with story.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>It feels a bit contradictory to say this book had a slow start, while still being a quick enjoyable read. I'd be hard pressed to say exactly what happened for most of the first part of this book of importance, but the rest of the book more than made up for that. Not to mention he does it in a way where it never feels rushed.<br/><br/>Mr. Cornwell just seems to be an ex</span>
  <span id="freeText8788995583591499896" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Another enjoyable read in this series. These books are always quick reads that seem so packed with story.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />It feels a bit contradictory to say this book had a slow start, while still being a quick enjoyable read. I'd be hard pressed to say exactly what happened for most of the first part of this book of importance, but the rest of the book more than made up for that. Not to mention he does it in a way where it never feels rushed.<br /><br />Mr. Cornwell just seems to be an expert and packing plot development and action into the minimum amount of words. You won't get flowerly prose, or excessive description. In return you're rewarded with a tight, and normally well-paced story.<br /><br />As with previous books, I continue to love Uthred and despise Alfred, but it's the secondary characters that make it for me. There are so many to note: Ragnar, Gisela, Brida, Steapa, Aethelfaed, Osferth, Father Pyrlig, Finan, and of course Brother Beocca. I'm especially fond of Ragnar and Steapa. This book is full of strong women in a time period where it seems the history books would have us believe none existed. I think he does an especially great job with Alfred's daughter Aethelfaed.<br /><br />Mr. Cornwell continues to blend history and fiction in such a way to leave me wondering how much is history and how much is fiction. These are always great stories. I'd read more history books if they were written by Mr. Cornwell. Despite knowing some of how things end up, I worry every time Uthred goes into battle.<br /><br />I want to jump right into the next book. Things don't exactly end up on a cliffhanger, but certainly there is much at hand to resolve. I fear for some of the things that may come to pass in the next book, but yet I can't wait to read it. I'll be sad when I catch up on this series because it's so enjoyable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8788995583591499896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer209968993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14992048826026413936">5 stars. It has to be. 5 stars for Uhtred of Bebbanburg, and 5 stars for his creator, Bernard Cornwell. <br/>It has been far too long between books in this Saxon series for me. I have had an Uhtred drought. So I hungered for this read when I came to it. And I am pleased to admit that it gave me everything I wanted and missed. <br/>If there are flaws in The Burning Land then I do not see them. That's not saying that there are none, but if there were, I failed to notice. I'll leave the flaws for others to p</span>
  <span id="freeText14992048826026413936" style="display:none">5 stars. It has to be. 5 stars for Uhtred of Bebbanburg, and 5 stars for his creator, Bernard Cornwell. <br />It has been far too long between books in this Saxon series for me. I have had an Uhtred drought. So I hungered for this read when I came to it. And I am pleased to admit that it gave me everything I wanted and missed. <br />If there are flaws in The Burning Land then I do not see them. That's not saying that there are none, but if there were, I failed to notice. I'll leave the flaws for others to pick through. I am just happy to be reading about Uhtred again, especially now that I have the next book, Death of Kings, sitting here waiting patiently for me.<br />Love the book, love the series (oh..except Sword Song..I didn't really like Sword Song).<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91807177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14525561319768272706">Alfred the Great, in Bernard Cornwell's Saxon Stories, has a love for order, peace, and Christianity. He has always been dismayed by his reliance on Uhtred, a pagan warrior who represents everything Alfred hates, but a reluctant bond of need held them loyal to each other. That bond snaps in "The Burning Land," when Alfred's punishing zeal is finally too much and Uhtred abandons his cause. Grieving for the death of his beloved wife, he flees north with thoughts of re-taking the fortress of his bi</span>
  <span id="freeText14525561319768272706" style="display:none">Alfred the Great, in Bernard Cornwell's Saxon Stories, has a love for order, peace, and Christianity. He has always been dismayed by his reliance on Uhtred, a pagan warrior who represents everything Alfred hates, but a reluctant bond of need held them loyal to each other. That bond snaps in "The Burning Land," when Alfred's punishing zeal is finally too much and Uhtred abandons his cause. Grieving for the death of his beloved wife, he flees north with thoughts of re-taking the fortress of his birthright. But oaths are not so easily abandoned, and Uhtred finds himself fighting alongside Alfred's redoubtable daughter Aethelflaed. Outnumbered against an army of Vikings and a vengeful witch, Uhtred scrambles for victory - and just possibly love. He is matured into a splendid lord of war, a man who effortlessly commands every battlefield, every room, and every page in which he appears. Alfred, Great or not, is an ungrateful bastard to snub such an ally, and it's marvelous to see him realize it. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7225446715086285316">rating: 4/5<br/><br/>Uhtred is a little older, a little wiser, a little less degrading to priests, and a little less prone to violence. <br/><br/>Okay, I lied.<br/><br/><i>"I'll hang him with his son's intestines," I said, "and piss on his corpse."</i><br/><br/>Ah, that's better!<br/><br/>He's just as bloody, foul-mouthed, and quick to temper while routinely shutting his brain down and acting before thinking (but he is a little older).   <span id="freeText7225446715086285316" style="display:none">rating: 4/5<br /><br />Uhtred is a little older, a little wiser, a little less degrading to priests, and a little less prone to violence. <br /><br />Okay, I lied.<br /><br /><i>"I'll hang him with his son's intestines," I said, "and piss on his corpse."</i><br /><br />Ah, that's better!<br /><br />He's just as bloody, foul-mouthed, and quick to temper while routinely shutting his brain down and acting before thinking (but he is a little older). Yup, exactly what I have come to expect from the series. <br /><br />With one drawback. The middle was a bit dry on the action, and a bit high on the Babbenburg whining. But BC made it up to us with an extraordinary major battle at the end. I love make-up battles (ranks high up there right next to make-up sex).<br /><br />Overall, loved it! <br /><br />And jut to whet your appetite, a little continuation of the Uhtred vs Alfred religious debate:<br /><br /><i>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["If its your God's will," I [Uhtred] said harshly, "then nothing I can do nor anything Edward can do will stop it."<br /><br />"We're not puppets in God's hands," he [Alfred] said testily. "We are his instruments. We earn our fate."..."Don't your gods reward you for good behavior?"<br /><br />"My gods are capricious, lord."<br /><br />"How can you serve a capricious god?" Alfred asked.<br /><br />"I don't."<br /><br />"But you said..."<br /><br />"They are capricious," I interrupted him, "but that's their pleasure. My task is not to serve them, but to amuse them, and if I do then they will reward me in the life to come."<br /><br />"Amuse them?" He sounded shocked.<br /><br />"Why not?" I demanded. "We have cats, dogs, and falcons for our pleasure, the gods made us for the same reason. Why did your God make you?"<br /><br />"To be his servant," he said firmly. "If I'm God's cat then I must catch the devil's mice. That is duty, Lord Uhtred, duty."<br /><br />"While my duty," I said, "is to catch Harald and slice his head off. That, I think, will amuse my gods."<br /><br />"Your gods are cruel," he said, then shuddered.<br /><br />"Men are cruel," I said, "and the gods made us like themselves, and some of the gods are kind, some are cruel. So are we. If it amuses the gods then Harald will slice my head off." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4805454771275184094"><blockquote> <b> I was without a lord. I was outcast. I was free. I was going Viking.</b>
</blockquote> *rubs hands together* Yes! Yes! Go Viking! <p> Uhtred didn't go Viking as much as promised, but he did run the oars! </p><p> <br/><img alt='kirk douglas -VIKINGS -RICHARD FLEISCHER-RUNNING THE OARS on Make ...' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593129227ra/29710021.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </p> <p> I don't know how he manages it, but Uhtred sure does get himself into a muddle. Sick, King Alfred is mighty pissed at Uhtred. What's new? </p> <p> <img alt='The Last Kingdom - Page 9 - Other Genre Television - PRIMETIMER' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593129227ra/29710019.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/></p> <p> I think the most important point in this story is that Æthelflæd is blossoming into Lady of the Mercians that history remembers. I really love her history and I love th</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4805454771275184094" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> I was without a lord. I was outcast. I was free. I was going Viking.</b>
</blockquote> *rubs hands together* Yes! Yes! Go Viking! <p> Uhtred didn't go Viking as much as promised, but he did run the oars! </p><p> <br><img alt="kirk douglas -VIKINGS -RICHARD FLEISCHER-RUNNING THE OARS on Make ..." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593129227ra/29710021.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </p> <p> I don't know how he manages it, but Uhtred sure does get himself into a muddle. Sick, King Alfred is mighty pissed at Uhtred. What's new? </p> <p> <img alt="The Last Kingdom - Page 9 - Other Genre Television - PRIMETIMER" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593129227ra/29710019.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></p> <p> I think the most important point in this story is that Æthelflæd is blossoming into Lady of the Mercians that history remembers. I really love her history and I love the way Bernard Cornwell has brought her to life. </p> <p> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1593129227i/29710020._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></p> <p> At this point, it's really no fair to compare the tv show to the book. The books are so overwhelmingly fantastic, and the show is having a hard time doing it justice. While the show is taking it's own turn, the book series is keeping true to the spirit of how life was during King Alfred's reign. Also, making sure history doesn't forget England's first warrior queen, Aethelflaed. <br></p></span>

    <a title="Krista Claudine Baetiong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13624574-krista-claudine-baetiong"><img alt="Krista Claudine Baetiong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552474554p2/13624574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1568381909?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista Claudine Baetiong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista Claudine Baetiong" href="/user/show/13624574-krista-claudine-baetiong">Krista Claudine Baetiong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13624574-krista-claudine-baetiong?shelf=period-medieval">period-medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13624574-krista-claudine-baetiong?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13624574-krista-claudine-baetiong?shelf=author-europe">author-europe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568381909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer274879124539012950">King Alfred of Wessex is gravely ill, Uhtred’s loyalty wavers yet again and goes where his fate leads him, the Danes are ever planning to thwart Alfred’s vision of <i>England</i>, Ætheling Edward is gradually proving himself to be a worthy successor, and the king’s daughter Æthelflæd, whose life is suddenly in peril, has found a formidable champion in Uhtred. Meanwhile, lands get burned, towns are sacked and its populace cut down or mutilated, battlefields are awash in gore, and Father Pyrlig, my favor</span>
  <span id="freeText274879124539012950" style="display:none">King Alfred of Wessex is gravely ill, Uhtred’s loyalty wavers yet again and goes where his fate leads him, the Danes are ever planning to thwart Alfred’s vision of <i>England</i>, Ætheling Edward is gradually proving himself to be a worthy successor, and the king’s daughter Æthelflæd, whose life is suddenly in peril, has found a formidable champion in Uhtred. Meanwhile, lands get burned, towns are sacked and its populace cut down or mutilated, battlefields are awash in gore, and Father Pyrlig, my favorite burly Welsh warrior-priest, remains a cheerful pragmatist in this world of doom.<br /><br />The battle scenes are, as always, explicitly and brutally gory; and war strategies, which Cornwell describes here in a flourish, always hold a fascinating afterthought for me. I don’t know, but I may as well be looking forever at a mass of land (be it a valley or a plain or whatever) and still be unable to pin down its pros and cons in an actual battle. So, yes, fictional Uhtred is a gem for living up to his reputation and ability as a great warrior (though he certainly relies on fate a lot!), and King Alfred’s excessive piousness I can overlook since his methodical ways and love of order have paved way for the existence of <i>burhs</i> or fortified towns—among other things—and greatly helped Wessex in repelling Viking attacks for a long time.<br /><br />I also enjoyed Uhtred’s relationship with his Dane <i>brother</i> Ragnar, and his unlikely fraternity with Finan (an Irish warrior and a former slave), Father Pyrlig (a Welsh priest), Osferth (the king’s bastard son), Sihtric (a half-Dane and his former servant) and Steapa (an impressive Saxon warrior who hates the Danes and whom Uhtred has fought once). It’s always a good read moment when these men bond, watch each other’s back, and show off their deadly warrior routines during a battle. And I find that I am enjoying this war series so far and would not really mind at all if the remaining books are as blood-spattered as this one is. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="274879124539012950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228340648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1760824-graham"><img alt="Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380743323p2/1760824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228340648?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graham" href="/user/show/1760824-graham">Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=anglo-saxon">anglo-saxon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=viking">viking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228340648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6885699463219204826">A great entry in the Saxon Stories by Bernard Cornwell. This is the fifth book and a return to the quality of the initial three after the slightly sub-standard SWORD SONG. This one's so great because it sees Uhtred finally breaking away from Alfred (hurrah!) and setting up power on his own.<br/><br/>Once again, the story is dominated with powerful descriptions of England's lands and peoples. Cornwell has great fun with a fictional villain - Harald Bloodhair, a man who lives up to his name before each batt</span>
  <span id="freeText6885699463219204826" style="display:none">A great entry in the Saxon Stories by Bernard Cornwell. This is the fifth book and a return to the quality of the initial three after the slightly sub-standard SWORD SONG. This one's so great because it sees Uhtred finally breaking away from Alfred (hurrah!) and setting up power on his own.<br /><br />Once again, the story is dominated with powerful descriptions of England's lands and peoples. Cornwell has great fun with a fictional villain - Harald Bloodhair, a man who lives up to his name before each battle - and culminates with one of the best battles of the series, an assault on a seemingly impervious fortress.<br /><br />As much as I love this series, I realise that the incessant bickering between Uhtred and Alfred/his cronies in the previous books was starting to grate. Cornwell had finished developing the relationships by the time of the second book, which is why they were so repetitive in SWORD SONG. THE BURNING LAND has Uhtred allying himself with characters both new (the beguiling Athelflaed) and old (the appealing Ragnar) which breaks up the mould and freshens everything up. Add in a truly horrible villainess - Skade - and you have the trappings of a rousing, breakneck historical adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6885699463219204826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7416068628623746373">This is my favorite after Lords of the North. Bernard Cornwell is much more than a master of battles, this book showed me he's also an expert of characterization. Mix that up with amazing story telling ability and you've got a gem.<br/><br/> The main reason I love this series? Uhtred is Amazing. And book after book Cornwell keeps fleshing him out and adding layers of complexity to him. Every experience he has adds or takes something from him. And the author has applied this rule to the minor characters as</span>
  <span id="freeText7416068628623746373" style="display:none">This is my favorite after Lords of the North. Bernard Cornwell is much more than a master of battles, this book showed me he's also an expert of characterization. Mix that up with amazing story telling ability and you've got a gem.<br /><br /> The main reason I love this series? Uhtred is Amazing. And book after book Cornwell keeps fleshing him out and adding layers of complexity to him. Every experience he has adds or takes something from him. And the author has applied this rule to the minor characters as well, which adds a great deal of realism and continuity to these books. <br /><br /> Some of my favorite minor characters: [Ragnar the Younger], friend and brother to Uhtred, and probably the happiest man i've read in book. Fearless and brutal in battle. Feared and loved...but no one throws a feast like Ragnar.<br />[Haesten], The villain you love to hate, all swagger and all smiles...but ever thinking two steps ahead. <br />King Alfred, the master manipulator. Steapa, Finan, Brida, Gisella, Father Beocca, Father Pyrlig, Osferth, Æthelflæd...<br /><br /> It's at the point in the series where the tension is building faster. I can't wait to see what happens next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7416068628623746373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_392973241" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6803829-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413944642p2/6803829.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392973241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8794799089436246760">5 books into this series and I'm still not feeling any burnout, which is somewhat rare for me with a (relatively) long series like this one. All the stuff that I assume that Cornwell fans like is still here in spades; thorough research, vivid painting of the British landscape, memorable characters, and insane battle sequences. Seriously, I can't believe those poor people had to live through such brutal fighting. I've never been in any kind of combat situation, but I have to imagine that fighting</span>
  <span id="freeText8794799089436246760" style="display:none">5 books into this series and I'm still not feeling any burnout, which is somewhat rare for me with a (relatively) long series like this one. All the stuff that I assume that Cornwell fans like is still here in spades; thorough research, vivid painting of the British landscape, memorable characters, and insane battle sequences. Seriously, I can't believe those poor people had to live through such brutal fighting. I've never been in any kind of combat situation, but I have to imagine that fighting with weapons like swords, spears, axes, etc. had to be a hell of a lot scarier and harder than with the advanced weaponry of today.<br /><br />One thing I noticed that Cornwell's developing nicely is the characterization. All of the characters seem a lot more fully fleshed out than in the first few books. This is the first time in the series that I've actually really <i>hated</i> one of the villains (Skade); even then, there were moments where the vulnerable, human side of her really came out and I momentarily felt badly for her, then she got back to her usual business of poking people's eyes out and stuff and I just needed her to die. This deeper look into the characters extends to Uhtred as well, there were several points in this book where he even comes off as somewhat of a kind person, which for a nice-guy wiener like myself was refreshing and pleasant.<br /><br />Aside from the sheer amount of entertainment I've gotten out of these books, I've also seriously bolstered my embarrassingly poor level of knowledge about the history of Britain and it's helped stoke my interest in this period of history. I've been recommending these books to everyone I can with even a slight interest in middle ages Britain and I can comfortably say that they have something for everyone (minus the people who are uncomfortable with reading about violence and turmoil, in which case you probably shouldn't be reading about any period in the middle ages).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8794799089436246760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

Plus, I found that Uhtred choices in women were not very wise and this annoyed me a bit <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[After Gisela's death, Skade first (but lust, I can understand even if the girl is a monster), and then Aethelflaed. Aethelflaed is well known (in the history of England) for fighting against the Danes so she had to be introduced as the leader she'll become.<br /><br />I love the 80 y/o Uhtred telling the story of his life and of the creation of England and I love it so much when he reflects on religion or on history or on life, love, lust, war... I'll keep reading about Uhtred even if he annoys me at times (for his choices, for his allegiances, for the oaths he, most unwillingly, gives ...) and I do hope that some day, he'll have Bebbanburg back.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RH6pGtoDpjJzOnO0cs5k6bcCQJlXBWIVWEWk+hnMvMqnyupzYiPDE8/X2B5Ibk28AKRPBynkrEk87YYroVhNxA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KFX+juM6YeaBL8jtmxU9Ke1PT+8lxh2EzSk6yiK8JuDL4b3nWxoExz3CY0ehtRR8WulAcVsn09ipgRgbmijX7g==')})
  }

A young boatbuilder\'s life is turned upside down when the only home he\'s ever known is raided by Vikings, forcing him and his family to move and start their lives anew in a small hamlet where he does not fit in. . . . A Norman noblewoman marries for love, following her husband across the sea to a new land, but the customs of her husband\'s homeland are shockingly different, and as she begins to realize that everyone around her is engaged in a constant, brutal battle for power, it becomes clear that a single misstep could be catastrophic. . . . A monk dreams of transforming his humble abbey into a center of learning that will be admired throughout Europe. And each in turn comes into dangerous conflict with a clever and ruthless bishop who will do anything to increase his wealth and power.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17679677504109022607\" href=\"#\" Conn Iggulden is just such a writer, bringing to vivid life one of the most fascinating eras in human history. In a true masterpiece of historical fiction, Iggulden takes us on a breathtaking journey through ancient Rome, sweeping us into a realm of tyrants and slaves, of dark intrigues and seething passions. What emerges is both a grand romantic tale of coming-of-age in the Roman Empire and a vibrant portrait of the early years of a man who would become the most powerful ruler on earth: Julius Caesar. On the lush Italian peninsula, a new empire is taking shape. At its heart is the city of Rome, a place of glory and decadence, beauty and bloodshed. Against this vivid backdrop, two boys are growing to manhood, dreaming of battles, fame, and glory in service of the mightiest empire the world has ever known. One is the son of a senator, a boy of privilege and ambition to whom much has been given and from whom much is expected. The other is a bastard child, a boy of strength and cunning, whose love for his adoptive family-and his adoptive brother-will be the most powerful force in his life. As young Gaius and Marcus are trained in the art of combat-under the tutelage of one of Rome\'s most fearsome gladiators-Rome itself is being rocked by the art of treachery and ambition, caught in a tug-of-war as two rival generals, Marius and Sulla, push the empire toward civil war. For Marcus, a bloody campaign in Greece will become a young soldier\'s proving ground. For Gaius, the equally deadly infighting of the Roman Senate will be the battlefield where he hones his courage and skill. And for both, the love of an extraordinary slave girl will be an honor each will covet but only one will win. The two friends are forced to walk different paths, and by the time they meet again everything will have changed. Both will have known love, loss, and violence. And the land where they were once innocent will be thrust into the grip of bitter conflict-a conflict that will set Roman against Roman...and put their friendship to the ultimate test. Brilliantly interweaving history and adventure, Conn Iggulden conjures a stunning array of contrasts-from the bloody stench of a battlefield to the opulence of the greatest city in history, from the tenderness of a lover to the treachery of an assassin.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell">About Bernard Cornwell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1504578807p3/12542.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/12542.Bernard_Cornwell">Bernard Cornwell
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
13,026
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8998558715028625044">Cornwell was born in London in 1944. His father was a Canadian airman, and his mother, who was English, a member of the Women's Auxiliary Air Force. He was adopted and brought up in Essex by the Wiggins family, who were members of the Peculiar People, a strict Protestant sect who banned frivolity of all kinds and even medicine. After he left them, he changed his name to his birth mother's maiden n</span>
  <span id="freeText8998558715028625044" style="display:none">Cornwell was born in London in 1944. His father was a Canadian airman, and his mother, who was English, a member of the Women's Auxiliary Air Force. He was adopted and brought up in Essex by the Wiggins family, who were members of the Peculiar People, a strict Protestant sect who banned frivolity of all kinds and even medicine. After he left them, he changed his name to his birth mother's maiden name, Cornwell.<br /><br />Cornwell was sent away to Monkton Combe School, attended the University of London, and after graduating, worked as a teacher. He attempted to enlist in the British armed services at least three times but was rejected on the grounds of myopia.<br /><br />He then joined BBC's Nationwide and was promoted to become head of current affairs at BBC Northern Ireland. He then joined Thames Television as editor of Thames News. He relocated to the United States in 1980 after marrying an American. Unable to get a green card, he started writing novels, as this did not require a work permit.<br /><br />As a child, Cornwell loved the novels of C.S. Forester, chronicling the adventures of fictional British naval officer Horatio Hornblower during the Napoleonic Wars, and was surprised to find there were no such novels following Lord Wellington's campaign on land. Motivated by the need to support himself in the U.S. through writing, Cornwell decided to write such a series. He named his chief protagonist Richard Sharpe, a rifleman involved in most major battles of the Peninsular War.<br /><br />Cornwell wanted to start the series with the Siege of Badajoz but decided instead to start with a couple of "warm-up" novels. These were <i>Sharpe's Eagle</i> and <i>Sharpe's Gold</i>, both published in 1981. <i>Sharpe's Eagle</i> was picked up by a publisher, and Cornwell got a three-book deal. He went on to tell the story of Badajoz in his third Sharpe novel, <i>Sharpe's Company</i>, published in 1982.<br /><br />Cornwell and wife Judy co-wrote a series of novels, published under the pseudonym "Susannah Kells". These were <i>A Crowning Mercy</i>, published in 1983, <i>Fallen Angels</i> in 1984, and <i>Coat of Arms</i> (aka <i>The Aristocrats</i>) in 1986. (Cornwell's strict Protestant upbringing informed the background of <i>A Crowning Mercy</i>, which took place during the English Civil War.) In 1987, he also published <i>Redcoat</i>, an American Revolutionary War novel set in Philadelphia during its 1777 occupation by the British.<br /><br />After publishing eight books in his ongoing Sharpe series, Cornwell was approached by a production company interested in adapting them for television. The producers asked him to write a prequel to give them a starting point to the series. They also requested that the story feature a large role for Spanish characters to secure co-funding from Spain. The result was <i>Sharpe’s Rifles</i>, published in 1987, and a series of Sharpe television films staring Sean Bean.<br /><br />A series of contemporary thrillers with sailing as a background and common themes followed: <i>Wildtrack</i> published in 1988, <i>Sea Lord</i> (aka <i>Killer's Wake</i>) in 1989, <i>Crackdown</i> in 1990, <i>Stormchild</i> in 1991, and <i>Scoundrel</i>, a political thriller, in 1992.<br /><br />In June 2006, Cornwell was made an Officer of the Order of the British Empire in the Queen's 80th Birthday Honours List.<br /><br />Cornwell's latest work, <i>Azincourt</i>, was released in the UK in October 2008. The protagonist is an archer who participates in the Battle of Agincourt, another devastating defeat suffered by the French in the Hundred Years War. However, Cornwell has stated that it will not be about Thomas of Hookton from The Grail Quest or any of his relatives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8998558715028625044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

The old enemy comes from Wessex where a dynastic struggle will determine who will be the next king.  And the new foe is Sköll, a Norseman, whose ambition is to be King of Northumbria and who leads a frightening army of wolf-warriors, men who fight half-crazed in the belief that they are indeed wolves. Uhtred, believing he is cursed, must fend off one enemy while he tries to destroy the other. In this new chapter of the Saxon Tales series—a rousing adventure of courage, treachery, duty, devotion, majesty, love and battle, as seen through the eyes of a warrior straddling two worlds—Uhtred
